data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_valence-%20and%20spin-state%20transformation%20of%20cobalt">valence- and spin-state transformation of cobalt</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium-ion+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium-ion%20batteries">sodium-ion batteries</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Cathode+Materials&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_cathode%20materials">cathode materials</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Post-lithium+Technologies&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_post-lithium%20technologies">post-lithium technologies</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Stationary+Energy+Storage&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_stationary%20energy%20storage">stationary energy storage</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">Recently, layered sodium-containing oxides have gained immense interest because of their applicability as electrode materials in sodium-ion batteries. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref2'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2" aria-label="reference 1 and 2">(1,2)</a> These compounds crystallize in three structure types (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>), depending on the synthesis conditions and the sodium content. From the structural point of view, sodium is coordinated either in an octahedral (O) or prismatic (P) oxygen environment, and the stacking sequence of oxygen layers yields the number of sheets within the unit cell. Usually, either two or three metal-oxide sheets per unit cell are present. Generally, the O3-phases are expected with the sodium content of 0.7 &lt; <i>x</i> &lt; 1, whereas the P2-type is often obtained at <i>x</i> ≈ 0.7 and the P3-type at <i>x</i> ≈ 0.5. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref2" aria-label="reference 2">(2)</a> As reported for Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>CoO<sub>2</sub> earlier, plenty of structural variations within the layered type can be obtained upon electrochemical desodiation, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3" aria-label="reference 3">(3)</a> which differ from each other not only by the amount of Na involved, but also by the stability of each layer and the kinetics affected by the local environment of Na. These complex phase transformations produce a steplike potential curve, which is detrimental for battery applications. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3" aria-label="reference 3">(3)</a></div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/medium/am-2018-11609g_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0001.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. P2- (a), P3- (b), and O3- (c) type structures of layered oxides of sodium and 3d transition metals, NaMO<sub>2</sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref2" aria-label="reference 2">(2)</a> Yellow spheres represent sodium atoms, whereas red spheres indicate oxygen positions. Transition metals are randomly distributed in the center of the blue oxygen octahedra.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11609&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">On the other hand, the diverse desodiated phases are remarkable for their interesting electronic properties such as variable magnetic states, charge-ordering effects, and dissimilar electric properties. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref4" aria-label="reference 4">(4)</a> At a high sodium content, the Seebeck coefficient increases, which renders the material promising for thermoelectric applications. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5 ref6'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref5 ref6" aria-label="reference 5 and 6">(5,6)</a> Furthermore, by intercalating water molecules into the interlayer space, superconductivity could be observed at temperatures below 5 K. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7 ref8'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7 ref8" aria-label="reference 7 and 8">(7,8)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">For applications of layered sodium oxides in Na-ion batteries, many efforts were made to study the cooperative effect of binary metals in metal-oxide layers via the partial replacement of the “high-voltage” metal cations such as Co by other transition metals.</div><div class="NLM_p">This strategy not only leads to a smooth potential curve but also delivers higher capacities and improves the stability upon cycling. The best results were achieved for the Mn/Fe, Mn/Ni, and Mn/Co pairs. For example, the reversible capacity of O3-type NaFeO<sub>2</sub> is limited to 90 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, and the synthesis of a P2-type is extremely difficult because of the instability of Fe<sup>4+</sup>. By replacing half of the iron with manganese prone to the formation of the 4+ valence state, a stabilized P2-type Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>[Fe<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>]O<sub>2</sub> is obtained that exhibits a capacity of 190 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9" aria-label="reference 9">(9)</a> The redox process is expected to be fully sustained by the Fe<sup>3+</sup>/Fe<sup>4+</sup> couple, whereas Mn is electrochemically inactive and simply stabilizes the structure. The substitution of Ni in O3-NaNiO<sub>2</sub> leads to either P2- or O3-type Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>[Ni<sub><i>y</i></sub>Mn<sub>1–<i>y</i></sub>]O<sub>2</sub>, which results in a smoother potential curve. The O3-type shows large capacities of up to 185 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> with poor reversibility, whereas the whole redox process is attributed to Ni<sup>2+</sup>/Ni<sup>4+</sup>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref10" aria-label="reference 10">(10)</a> In comparison, the P2-type delivers only 86 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> with an excellent reversibility (2.0–4.0 V vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na). Using a broader cycling range (1.6–3.8 V vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na) results in capacities up to 135 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> with inferior reversibility. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref11" aria-label="reference 11">(11)</a> These findings show that the potential window for cycling the layered oxides has to be carefully adjusted until a compromise between larger capacity and long-term stability is reached.</div><div class="NLM_p">For P2-Na<sub>2/3</sub>Mn<sub><i>y</i></sub>Co<sub>1–<i>y</i></sub>O<sub>2</sub>, the substitution of Co by Mn increases the capacities from 115 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at <i>y</i> = 0 to 164 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at <i>y</i> = 1 with a simultaneously reduced cycling stability. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12" aria-label="reference 12">(12)</a> The low reversibility was attributed to a passivating layer formed by Mn, although no further details about this layer are provided. At high manganese contents, Mn<sup>4+</sup>/Mn<sup>3+</sup> is assumed to contribute to the redox process, as an additional capacity at lower voltages is observed.</div><div class="NLM_p">The partial substitution of Co/Ni by Ti has been less studied till date, although Ti offers several advantages, particularly (i) structural stability while maintaining low weight, (ii) an additional capacity at low potentials, and (iii) sustainability. Ti is prone to the formation of the 4+ state and can stabilize the desodiated structure regarding numerous phase transformations, as reported for layered isostructural Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>TiS<sub>2</sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13" aria-label="reference 13">(13)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">On the basis of Mn-substituted O3-NaNiO<sub>2</sub>, the partial replacement of Mn(IV) by the lighter Ti(IV) in NaNi<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.3</sub>Ti<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> was found to increase the gravimetric capacities. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14" aria-label="reference 14">(14)</a> Using Ti as the only substituent in the absence of Mn also led to a high capacity, cycling stability and rate capability, as reported for O3-type NaNi<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13" aria-label="reference 13">(13)</a> and P2-type NaCo<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15" aria-label="reference 15">(15)</a> The presence of Ti leads to smooth potential changes upon (de)sodiation, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref16" aria-label="reference 16">(16)</a> and a smaller volume change has also been assumed. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref2" aria-label="reference 2">(2)</a> Moreover, Ti(IV) can be reduced to Ti(III), providing an additional electrochemical capacity. In O3-Na<sub>0.8</sub>Ni<sub>0.4</sub>Ti<sub>0.6</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, the redox couples Ni<sup>4+</sup>/Ni<sup>2+</sup> at 3.5 V and Ti<sup>4+</sup>/Ti<sup>3+</sup> at 0.7 V were identified, which offer the possibility of designing symmetrical cells. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref17" aria-label="reference 17">(17)</a> Additionally, Ti, as the ninth most abundant element in the Earth’s crust, is known to be environmentally compatible and lightweight, which makes it favorable to replace Co, Ni, and Mn to develop environmentally friendly and sustainable technologies and reduce the usage of rare and toxic elements. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18 ref19'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18 ref19" aria-label="reference 18 and 19">(18,19)</a> A major obstacle in this road is the absence of detailed structural investigations of the sodiation and desodiation processes in Ti-doped compounds. Moreover, only the O3- and P2-type forms have been tested in sodium-ion batteries so far. The P3-form was only recorded as an unstable intermediate formed upon electrochemical desodiation. The targeted synthesis of P3-type layered compounds could open up a completely new approach for these materials.</div><div class="NLM_p last">In this work, we synthesized the O3- and P3-forms of Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and tested these novel materials in electrochemical cells. Changes in their crystal and electronic structures upon electrochemical Na removal and insertion are studied in operando using synchrotron powder diffraction and X-ray absorption spectroscopy (XAS). For the O3-type form, we observed phase transformation into the P3-type upon desodiation, whereas no structural changes other than conventional unit cell volume shrinkage were detected for Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> of the P3-type.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">Experimental Section</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec2_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4"> Synthesis and Characterization</h3><div class="NLM_p">P3-Na<sub>0.65</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and O3-Na<sub>0.95</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> were prepared by solid-state reactions using stoichiometric amounts of Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> and Co(CH<sub>3</sub>COO)<sub>2</sub>·4H<sub>2</sub>O (Fluka, &gt;99.0%). Pellets made from the reactants were placed in alumina crucibles and heated up to 930 °C for 25 h in air and quenched to room temperature from 800 °C. The P3 modification was obtained by subsequent annealing to 400 °C or by slow cooling of 0.5 °C/min from the synthesis temperature. After heat treatment, the samples were immediately transferred to an argon-filled glovebox.</div><div class="NLM_p last">For phase analysis, powder X-ray diffraction (XRD) was carried out using a STOE STADI P diffractometer with Co Kα<sub>1</sub> radiation (λ = 1.78896 Å) in the transmission mode. To avoid air contact, the samples were sealed between polyimide sheets.</div></div><div id="sec2_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i5"> High-Temperature Synchrotron and Neutron Powder Diffraction (NPD) Studies</h3><div class="NLM_p">Temperature-dependent synchrotron powder diffraction experiments were performed at the ID22 beamline of the ESRF, Grenoble [λ = 0.35422(1) Å] in the high-resolution mode. The P3-Na<sub>0.65</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and O3-Na<sub>0.95</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> samples were measured in sealed quartz capillaries between 25 and 900 °C. The sample temperature was controlled by the hot-air blower.</div><div class="NLM_p last">Elastic coherent NPD was performed using a high-resolution powder diffractometer SPODI at the research reactor FRM-II (Garching, Germany) with monochromatic neutrons at λ = 1.5481(1) Å wavelength. Measurements were performed in the zero-field in the Debye–Scherrer geometry. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20" aria-label="reference 20">(20)</a> The powdered O3-Na<sub>0.85</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> sample (ca. 2 cm<sup>3</sup>) was filled into a thick-walled (1.5 mm) quartz tube of 10 mm diameter and then mounted in a high-temperature oven. Powder diffraction data were collected in air between 25 and 800 °C and then corrected for geometrical aberrations and the curvature of the Debye–Scherrer rings. For both diffraction studies, the structural parameters were determined by Rietveld analysis based on all available reflections using the program Fullprof implemented in the WinPLOTR software. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a></div></div><div id="sec2_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i6" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i6"> Electrochemical Investigations</h3><div class="NLM_p">Electrochemical tests were performed in two-electrode Swagelok-type cells using a VMP3 potentiostat (Biologic Instruments). Electrodes were prepared by pressing a mixture of the active material with Super P carbon (BASF) and polytetrafluoroethylene (PTFE, Aldrich) in the 80:10:10 weight ratio onto an aluminum current collector. Home-made sodium anodes were prepared by rolling pieces of metallic sodium (Alfa Aesar, 99.95%) into plates and cutting out disks. A glass fiber cloth (Whatman, GF/D), soaked with electrolyte, served as the separator. The influence of various home-made electrolytes was investigated. Hence, NaClO<sub>4</sub> (ACS, 98.0–102.0%) and NaPF<sub>6</sub> (ABCR, 99.0%) salts were dissolved in propylene carbonate (PC, BASF) or a mixture of ethylene carbonate (EC, BASF) and dimethyl carbonate (DMC, BASF). Galvanostatic cycling with potential limitation (GCPL) was carried out in various potential windows at C/10, where C denotes the current necessary to insert 1 Na per formula unit within 1 h.</div><div class="NLM_p last">For galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) experiments, three-electrode Swagelok-type cells with metallic sodium were used as both counter and reference electrodes. A current of C/20 was applied for 10 min, where C corresponds to the current needed for the insertion or extraction of 1 Na per formula unit within 1 h. Before the next titration step, there was a rest period of 12 h to allow the determination of the open-circuit voltage (OCV) value near equilibrium conditions. Chemical diffusion coefficients were calculated according to <span class="NLM_inline-formula"><i class="MathJaxEquation"></i><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer inline-formula-styles" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/medium/am-2018-11609g_m001.gif" alt="" id="_i7"></span> where <i>m</i> denotes the mass of the active material, <i>M</i> is its molar mass, <i>V</i><sub>m</sub> is the molar volume, and <i>A</i> is the electrode surface area. Δ<i>E</i><sub>s</sub> corresponds to the difference in the OCV between two titration steps, and τ denotes the duration of the applied current pulses. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref22" aria-label="reference 22">(22)</a></div></div><div id="sec2_4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i8" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i8"> X-ray Photoelectron Spectroscopy (XPS)</h3><div class="NLM_p last">For XPS studies of P3-Na<sub>0.65</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and O3-Na<sub>0.95</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, a PHI 5600 CI system with an Al Kα monochromatized X-ray source at 350 W and a hemispherical analyzer at a pass energy of 29 eV were used. The system base pressure was about 10<sup>–9</sup> mbar. Low-energy electrons were used to minimize surface charging. The binding energy scale was corrected with respect to the C 1s peak position of adventitious carbon at 284.8 eV.</div></div><div id="sec2_5" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i9" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i9"> Operando X-ray Synchrotron Diffraction</h3><div class="NLM_p last">Operando X-ray synchrotron diffraction measurements were conducted at PETRA III, beamline P02.1 (DESY, Hamburg, Germany). An eight-fold coin cell holder, connected to a Biologic Instruments potentiostat, was applied as described in the earlier work from our group. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a> A wavelength of 0.20718(1) and 0.20701(1) Å was determined by a refinement from the reflections of the LaB<sub>6</sub> reference material. For characterization of pristine materials, the first diffraction pattern was recorded before starting the electrochemical measurement. Subsequently, the cells were charged and discharged at a constant current. All diffraction patterns were analyzed by the Rietveld method using Fullprof. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a> Reflections of the Al current collector served as an internal standard during the measurements, and the refined lattice parameter of Al provided an independent control of the reliability of the obtained model parameters.</div></div><div id="sec2_6" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i10" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i10"> Operando X-ray Absorption Measurements</h3><div class="NLM_p last">Operando X-ray absorption experiments were carried out at the beamline P65 at PETRA III extension (DESY, Hamburg, Germany) in transmission and fluorescence setup. As described for the in situ XRD measurements, a coin cell holder, coupled with a Biologic Instruments potentiostat, was used for electrochemical cycling. For extended X-ray absorption fine structure (EXAFS) data analysis, the measured spectrum below the pre-edge was fitted linearly, whereas the postedge background contribution was fitted to a quadratic polynomial. This background μ<sub>o</sub>(<i>E</i>) was subtracted from the absorption spectrum μ(<i>E</i>), and the resulting data were normalized according to χ(<i>E</i>) = {μ(<i>E</i>) – μ<sub>0</sub>(<i>E</i>)}/Δμ<sub>0</sub>(<i>E</i>), where Δμ<sub>0</sub>(<i>E</i>) denotes the measured jump in absorption at the edge. The normalized spectrum was converted into <i>k</i> space using <i>k</i> = [2<i>m</i>(<i>E</i> – <i>E</i><sub>0</sub>)/ℏ<sup>2</sup>]<sup>1/2</sup>. By weighting χ(<i>k</i>) with <i>k</i><sup>3</sup>, contributions of higher <i>k</i> space were amplified. The resulting <i>k</i><sup>3</sup>χ(<i>k</i>) was Fourier-transformed into the <i>R</i> space, allowing the determination of bond contributions. Least-square fits were performed using the FEFF6 code. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24" aria-label="reference 24">(24)</a></div></div><div id="sec2_7" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i11" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i11"> Magnetization Measurements</h3><div class="NLM_p last">Magnetization measurements of pristine P3-Na<sub>0.65</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and O3-Na<sub>0.95</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and products of desodiation/sodiation were performed using a SQUID magnetometer (MPMS) from Quantum Design. The temperature dependences of magnetization were measured both in zero-field-cooled and in field-cooled modes between <i>T</i> = 2 and 330 K at 6 T. Magnetic susceptibilities in the paramagnetic region were analyzed in terms of the modified Curie–Weiss law with a temperature-independent paramagnetic contribution χ<sub>0</sub>: χ = <i>C</i>/(<i>T</i> – θ) + χ<sub>0</sub>, where the Curie constant <i>C</i> = <i>N</i><sub>A</sub>μ<sub>eff</sub><sup>2</sup>/3<i>k</i><sub>B</sub> yields the paramagnetic effective moment, μ<sub>eff</sub>.</div></div></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i12">Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec3_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i13" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i13"> Stability Field and Characterization of Different Structural Forms</h3><div class="NLM_p">Solid-state synthesis of Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> led to the formation of different products depending on the slight variation in the synthesis conditions such as air or pure O<sub>2</sub> atmosphere, fast or slow cooling, and changing the reaction time. In the literature, a significant vapor pressure over solid or liquid Na<sub>2</sub>O above 900 °C was reported, and an evaporation rate of “Na<sub>2</sub>O” of 8.61 g cm<sup>–2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup> at 840 °C was measured. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25" aria-label="reference 25">(25)</a> It would correspond to more than 4 g for 15 h in an open system. Because of the lower chemical potential of “Na<sub>2</sub>O” in Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, the partial pressure of the Na species must also be lower. It is noted that the sodium content in the material depends strongly on the reaction time at high temperatures.</div><div class="NLM_p">We succeeded in synthesizing layered phases in air, whereas a mixture of spinel and layered phases was observed after annealing the “NaCo<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub>” composition in the O<sub>2</sub> stream. The layered Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> phase with the <i>R</i>3̅<i>m</i> symmetry (O3-modification) forms after the synthesis in air at 930 °C during 15 h, followed by fast quenching of the sample from 800 °C. The experimental XRD pattern of such a sample, together with the calculated one on the basis of the α-NaFeO<sub>2</sub> structural model, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26" aria-label="reference 26">(26)</a> is presented in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>.</div><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/medium/am-2018-11609g_0008.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0008.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. Powder XRD patterns of O3- (<i>R</i>3̅<i>m</i>) and P3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (<i>R</i>3<i>m</i>) materials with the observed (red dots) and calculated (black solid line) curves together with their difference curves (blue solid line) and Bragg positions given as green vertical lines. The structural models for calculations using the Fullprof software <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a> are mentioned in the text.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0008.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11609&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">Additional annealing of this material in air at 400–600 °C for 20–30 h or very slow cooling from the synthesis temperature leads to the phase transformation into the P3-modification (<i>R</i>3<i>m</i> symmetry), which is accompanied by a shift of metal–oxygen layers with respect to each other (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>b). The experimental and theoretical XRD patterns of P3 are presented in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>. The theoretical pattern was calculated using the structural model of P3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>CoO<sub>2</sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27" aria-label="reference 27">(27)</a> Chemical analysis revealed the Na-rich Na<sub>0.95(2)</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> composition for the O3-form, whereas the Na-deficient Na<sub>0.65(2)</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> composition was detected for the P3 material. Detailed structural parameters are given in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/suppl_file/am8b11609_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S1</a>. XPS analysis of both forms together with CoO as Co<sup>2+</sup> reference indicates the presence of mostly Co<sup>2+</sup> in the O3-phase and Co<sup>3+</sup> in the P3-phase. The Co 2p core level spectrum of O3-Na<sub>0.95</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> shows the Co 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and Co 2p<sub>1/2</sub> main peaks at 779.1 and 794.6 eV, respectively, and intense satellite structures lying about 6 eV higher in energy (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>), similar to the CoO reference material. The Co 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and Co 2p<sub>1/2</sub> main peaks of P3-Na<sub>0.65</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> appear at 779.3 and 794.3 eV, whereas the satellite peaks in contrast to O3-Na<sub>0.95</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and CoO are less intensive and located about 10 eV higher in energy. It is common that the maxima of the Co 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and Co 2p<sub>1/2</sub> peaks are nearly the same for Co<sup>2+</sup>, Co<sup>3+</sup>, and Co<sup>4+</sup>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28 ref29'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref29" aria-label="reference 28 and 29">(28,29)</a> The intense satellite structure of Co<sup>2+</sup> in the Co 2p photoelectron spectra are found at 6 eV higher in energy, resulting from the charge-transfer-type screening on the Co 2p core hole, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30" aria-label="reference 30">(30)</a> which is a fingerprint of divalent Co in oxides. By contrast, the well-known low-spin (LS) Co<sup>3+</sup> material LiCoO<sub>2</sub> shows a much weaker satellite structure with the energy separation of about 10 eV between the main peak and the satellite peak. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28" aria-label="reference 28">(28)</a> Because the Co 2p<sub>3/2</sub> satellite peak in P3-Na<sub>0.65</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> shows considerably less intensity than in CoO and a shift of the main peak for more than 9 eV, the contribution of Co<sup>3+</sup> seems to be reasonable.</div><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/medium/am-2018-11609g_0009.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0009.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. Room temperature Co 2p photoelectron spectra of the P3- and O3-forms of Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> together with the Co<sup>2+</sup> reference material, CoO. The energy difference between Co 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and Co 2p<sub>1/2</sub> of about 15.3 eV and between Co 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and the satellite peak of 6.2 eV is typical for oxides with Co<sup>2+</sup>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30 ref31'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30 ref31" aria-label="reference 30 and 31">(30,31)</a> whereas the energy difference is 10 eV between Co 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and satellite peaks for Co<sup>3+</sup>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28" aria-label="reference 28">(28)</a></p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0009.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11609&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">High-temperature synchrotron powder diffraction and NPD experiments provided information about the phase transformation of O3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> into P3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> in air upon heating. New reflections of the P3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub>-phase are visible in the neutron diffraction patterns of O3-Na<sub>0.85</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> above 550 °C, especially in the 2θ region between 40 and 80°; see <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>a. The O3-Na<sub>0.95</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub>-phase with the higher Na content transforms into P3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> at about 900 °C.</div><figure id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/medium/am-2018-11609g_0010.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0010.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. (a) Temperature evolution of NPD patterns of O3-Na<sub>0.85</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub>. Above 550 °C, reflections of the P3-phase appear in the 2θ region between 40° and 80°, reflecting the phase transformation O3 → P3. (b). Temperature dependence of cell parameters and average (Co,Ti)–O interatomic distances for O3- and P3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, from NPD and synchrotron powder diffraction experiments upon heating. The new P3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, marked with red triangles, arises from O3-Na<sub>0.85</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> above 550 °C.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0010.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11609&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p last">The decrease in the Na content when going from the O3 to P3 structure leads to a shorter lattice parameter <i>a</i> and a larger lattice parameter <i>c</i>; see <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>b. Another effect of the higher Na content involves larger average (Co,Ti)–O distances, in agreement with the XPS observations, because the Na-rich materials contain more high-spin (HS)-Co<sup>2+</sup> with a larger ionic radius (0.745 Å) compared to HS-Co<sup>3+</sup> (0.61 Å) or LS-Co<sup>3+</sup> (0.545 Å). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32" aria-label="reference 32">(32)</a></div></div><div id="sec3_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i14" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i14"> Electrochemical Characterization in Na-Ion Batteries</h3><div class="NLM_p">Because a significant Na-deficiency was observed in the P3-form compared to the O3 one, and a temperature-induced transformation from O3 to P3 occurs, these materials can serve as hosts for Na extraction and insertion. In fact, both O3 and P3 structures show electrochemical activity in Na-ion batteries. Their first charging–discharging curve at different temperatures are compared in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>. In the temperature region between −5 and 40 °C, each modification shows a nearly temperature-independent behavior in the 2.0–4.2 V potential window, which is commonly chosen for cathode materials: a single-slope curve in the case of P3 and a two-step process for O3. Both materials demonstrate a charging capacity of 120–150 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, whereas only half of this value, about 65–70 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, is achieved during cell discharging.</div><figure id="fig5" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/medium/am-2018-11609g_0011.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0011.jpeg" id="gr5" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. Temperature dependence of the first charging–discharging cycle for (a) P3 (<i>R</i>3<i>m</i>) and (b) O3 (<i>R</i>3̅<i>m</i>) modifications of Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0011.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11609&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">In the case of the O3-form, the electrochemical curve at 55 °C differs from experiments at lower temperatures, providing higher capacity values upon cell discharging. Similarities in the discharging curves for both forms suggest a similar Na intercalation process.</div><div class="NLM_p">Testing of other electrolytes in the cells, for example, 1 M NaPF<sub>6</sub> in EC/DMC with the O3 and P3 cathodes, provides nearly the same values for the charging and much smaller values for the discharging capacities. Therefore, a discrepancy between the charging and discharging capacities may originate from side reactions in the electrochemical cells as well as from crystallographic and/or electronic transitions in the layered materials upon Na removal and insertion. Galvanostatic cycling results are given in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/suppl_file/am8b11609_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1</a>.</div><div class="NLM_p">Interestingly, the discharging capacity can be increased up to the level of the charging capacity if the cutoff cell voltage is reduced down to 0.2 V versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>). XRD analysis of the P3 and O3 materials after the first charging and subsequent discharging down to 0.2 V showed the presence of the two O3 and P3 structures in both materials without any hint of structural decomposition; see <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/suppl_file/am8b11609_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2</a>. Therefore, Na insertion into O3 and P3 is intertwined with a kinetically impeded transformation in both materials.</div><figure id="fig6" data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 6</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/medium/am-2018-11609g_0012.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0012.jpeg" id="gr6" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 6. Galvanostatic cycling of the O3- and P3-phases for the first and fifth cycles in the potential window 4.2–0.2 V vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na. For the initial P3-phase, a “constant voltage” mode was additionally applied at the end of cell discharging until the residual current reached 10% of the initial value.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0012.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11609&amp;id=fig6"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">Such a transformation must be clearly visible in chemical Na diffusion coefficients, which were evaluated for both materials using the GITT.</div><div class="NLM_p">In the P3 material, the chemical diffusion coefficients of Na span 4 orders of magnitude between 10<sup>–18</sup> and 10<sup>–14</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup> upon cell charging and discharging, whereas for the O3-form, a slightly smaller range is observed (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>). For the O3-form, an irregularity in the curve development was observed during charging between 2.55 and 2.75 V versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na that corresponds to the pronounced plateau during galvanostatic cycling (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>). With further charging, no considerable extreme values were measured for both materials. During subsequent cell discharging, no irregularity was detected for O3 down to 2.3 versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na, from which we conclude that the processes taking place during charging are not reversed at the corresponding discharging potentials. Furthermore, below 2.5 V versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na, Na diffusion coefficients strongly deteriorate in both materials, resulting in kinetically hindered sodiation in this potential range. Extending the GITT measurement to lower potentials was not successful, as (i) the potential rises back to values higher than 2 V versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na during the relaxation time and (ii) the polarization is so large that, even when applying extremely weak currents, a potential drop to 0 V versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na occurs.</div><figure id="fig7" data-index="7" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 7</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/medium/am-2018-11609g_0013.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0013.jpeg" id="gr7" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 7. Chemical diffusion coefficients of Na<sup>+</sup> in (a) P3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and (b) O3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, obtained by GITT measurements during the first charging–discharging cycle.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0013.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11609&amp;id=fig7"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec3_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i15" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i15"> Operando Evaluation of Crystallographic and Electronic Changes in Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> upon Na Extraction and Insertion</h3><div class="NLM_p last">To understand the origin of the high cell overpotential between charging and discharging, an evaluation of crystallographic and electronic structures is required. To this end, we performed operando synchrotron powder XRD and XAS studies of the P3- and O3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathodes in electrochemical test cells.</div></div><div id="sec3_4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i16" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i16"> Structural Characterization of Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> with Synchrotron Powder Diffraction</h3><div class="NLM_p">From the structural point of view, electrochemical Na removal from O3- and P3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> proceeds very similarly. The comparison of Bragg reflections for both materials upon cell charging and discharging with C/20 (1 Na inserted or extracted for 20 h) leads to the following conclusion (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">8</a>): upon Na extraction from the O3-Na<sub>0.95</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathode, a P3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> structure appears as a second phase shortly after the start of the desodiation process, whereas the initial O3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> disappears completely after several hours. This two-phase process in the O3 material, corresponding to the first plateau at about 2.7–2.8 V versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na, is clearly indicated by the vanishing 003 Bragg reflection intensity of the O3-phase at <i>d</i> = 5.37 Å and the growth of the 003 Bragg reflection of the P3-phase at <i>d</i> = 5.60 Å; see <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">8</a>a. After O3-Na<sub>0.95</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> completely disappeared, further desodiation up to 4.4 V and subsequent sodiation down to 1.2 V versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na occurs via a solid-solution mechanism because no new Bragg reflections appear. The O3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> structure does not reappear when the cutoff voltage is at 1.2 V. The Na extraction from P3-Na<sub>0.65</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and the subsequent Na insertion down to 1.2 V also proceed via a solid-solution mechanism. However, further decrease of the cell voltage below 1 V in either of the O3 or P3 initial materials is accompanied by the formation of the O3 structure in both materials. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">8</a>b shows the development of the 003 reflection of the O3-phase at the end of cell discharging for the pristine P3 material.</div><figure id="fig8" data-index="8" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 8</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/medium/am-2018-11609g_0014.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0014.jpeg" id="gr8" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 8. Part of the operando synchrotron powder diffraction data as contour plots from (a) O3-Na<sub>0.95</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (<i>R</i>3̅<i>m</i>) and (b) P3-Na<sub>0.65</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (<i>R</i>3<i>m</i>) as cathodes in electrochemical cells with the Na anode during galvanostatic cycling at C/20 (right) and voltage profile of the in situ cells vs time (left). Upon sodiation of both materials down to 1.2 V, the P3 structure is stable, whereas a decrease of the cell voltage below 1 V is accompanied by the formation of the O3 structure. The rectangles indicate the position of the 003 reflection for both phases.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0014.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11609&amp;id=fig8"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The quality of the obtained diffraction data allowed to follow the changes of the lattice parameters and the average (Co,Ti)–O interatomic distances during cell charging and discharging for both materials, using the Rietveld method. Moreover, for P3-Na<sub>0.65</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, the sodium content was also continuously refined and compared with the Na amount from the galvanostatic cycling measurements.</div><div class="NLM_p">As mentioned above, sodium extraction from the O3-phase quickly leads to the formation of the P3-phase, which shows a much shorter lattice parameter <i>a</i> and a longer lattice parameter <i>c</i>; see <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig9" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig9" id="" class=" internalNav">9</a>. This observation is consistent with the temperature-induced phase transformation O3 → P3, as discussed in the <a class="ref internalNav" href="#sec2_1" aria-label="Synthesis and Characterization">Synthesis and Characterization</a> section. For the initial P3-phase, the lattice parameters <i>a</i> and <i>c</i> are well in agreement with the values of the P3-phase formed during desodiation of the O3-phase. The changes in the corresponding unit cell volumes are shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/suppl_file/am8b11609_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3</a>.</div><figure id="fig9" data-index="9" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 9</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/medium/am-2018-11609g_0015.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0015.jpeg" id="gr9" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 9. Changes in the lattice parameters of O3- and P3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> upon Na removal (cell charging) and insertion (cell discharging). The Na content was extracted from the amount of current that passed through the cell during the galvanostatic experiment.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0015.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11609&amp;id=fig9"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">In both O3- and P3-forms, the lattice parameter <i>a</i> correlates with the average (Co,Ti)–O distance within transition metal–oxygen layers, whereas parameter <i>c</i> reflects the distance between the layers. Upon Na extraction, we observed a strong decrease in the lattice parameter <i>a</i> for the P3-phase at the beginning of the desodiation process for 0.65 ≥ <i>x</i>(Na) ≥ 0.50. This observation is associated with the oxidation of the residual amount of Co<sup>2+</sup> to Co<sup>3+</sup>, which must be present according to the charge distribution in Na<sub>0.65</sub>Co<sup>2+</sup><sub>0.15</sub>Co<sup>3+</sup><sub>0.35</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub>. The volume of the CoO<sub>6</sub> octahedra calculated from the ionic radii of oxygen and cobalt in different valences and spin states <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32" aria-label="reference 32">(32)</a> decreases drastically from HS-Co<sup>2+</sup> (13.16 Å<sup>3</sup>) to HS-Co<sup>3+</sup> (10.82 Å<sup>3</sup>) and LS-Co<sup>3+</sup> (9.81 Å<sup>3</sup>). Upon further Na removal with <i>x</i>(Na) ≤ 0.50, a mixture of Co<sup>3+</sup> and Co<sup>4+</sup> must form in the structure. The volume of Co<sup>4+</sup>O<sub>6</sub> (9.59 Å<sup>3</sup>) is only slightly smaller than the volume of LS-Co<sup>3+</sup>O<sub>6</sub>, but less noticeable than that of Ti<sup>4+</sup>O<sub>6</sub> (10.75 Å<sup>3</sup>). Hence, a combination of HS-Co<sup>3+</sup>O<sub>6</sub> and Ti<sup>4+</sup>O<sub>6</sub> should be the most appropriate at the Na<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> stoichiometry based on the geometrical criteria. However, the average (Co,Ti–O) distances for P3 revealed a value of about 1.95 Å, which is usually measured in oxide compounds with LS-Co<sup>3+</sup>; <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref33" aria-label="reference 33">(33)</a> see <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig10" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig10" id="" class=" internalNav">10</a>. This observation fits also well with a calculated value of 1.945 Å for a sum of the ionic radii of LS-Co<sup>3+</sup> and O<sup>2–</sup>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32" aria-label="reference 32">(32)</a> although strains may arise in the structure because the distance of 1.95 Å is too short for a conventional Ti–O bond length of 2.01 Å in the octahedral oxygen surrounding. Therefore, we can suppose a rather unexpected scenario with a coexistence of Ti<sup>4+</sup> and LS-Co<sup>3+</sup> in the Na<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> composition of the P3 structure.</div><figure id="fig10" data-index="10" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 10</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/medium/am-2018-11609g_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0002.jpeg" id="gr10" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 10. Changes in the average Co/Ti–O distances of the O3- and P3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> pristine materials upon Na removal and insertion. The Na content was calculated from the amount of current that passed through the cell during the galvanostatic experiment.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11609&amp;id=fig10"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The <i>c</i> parameter in the P3-phase grows upon Na removal because of the increased repulsion between the two neighboring oxygen layers, which would otherwise collide when the Na ions are removed.</div><div class="NLM_p">In the O3-phase, the average (Co,Ti)–O bond length of about 2.05 Å before the desodiation process is due to a combination of HS-Co<sup>2+</sup>–O and Ti<sup>4+</sup>–O with a small contribution of HS-Co<sup>3+</sup>–O, well in agreement with the calculated value of 2.068 Å based on the ionic radii. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32" aria-label="reference 32">(32)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">Upon desodiation, the mixture of HS-Co<sup>2+</sup>/HS-Co<sup>3+</sup>/Ti<sup>4+</sup> seems to be less stable than LS-Co<sup>3+</sup>/Ti<sup>4+</sup> because the P3-phase appears shortly after the Na removal starts. For the O3-phase, we observed only weak changes in the lattice parameters <i>a</i> and <i>c</i> with the Na content, indicating an immediate transformation into the P3-form. Note that during Na removal from O3 and P3 up to 4.2 V versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na, the Na compositions extracted from GCPL differ significantly for the resulting P3-phase, although the lattice parameters are almost the same. This behavior points to the occurrence of side reactions in the cells. A plot of the Na content obtained from the Rietveld analysis for P3 versus the Na content calculated from the current flow in the galvanostatic electrochemical experiment confirms this suggestion (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/suppl_file/am8b11609_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S4</a>).</div><div class="NLM_p last">During deep cell discharging of the initial P3 cathode, reflections of the O3-phase appear at the total <i>x</i>(Na) content of 0.33 calculated from the total current flow in the galvanostatic experiment. The average (Co,Ti)–O distances of both phases for the same sodium content differ significantly (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig10" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig10" id="" class=" internalNav">10</a>), clearly indicating different spin states of Co in both compounds. However, even the synchrotron diffraction data are insufficient to reliably distinguish between the sodium contents in both phases.</div></div><div id="sec3_5" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i17" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i17"> Operando Spectroscopic Characterization of O3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>TiO<sub>2</sub>: Revealing the Valence State of Cobalt</h3><div class="NLM_p">To evaluate the charge compensation in Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> upon desodiation, we have measured the Co K-edge of O3-Na<sub>0.95</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> in operando during electrochemical Na extraction and insertion; see the Co-K XAS spectra and enlarged pre-edge region together with Co, CoO, and Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> reference materials in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig11" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig11" id="" class=" internalNav">11</a>a. All spectra are normalized to unity step in the absorption coefficient μ. It is well-known that the valence state of the 3d transition metal is directly correlated with the position of the absorption edge E, defined at μ = 0.8. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29 ref33'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29 ref33" aria-label="reference 29 and 33">(29,33)</a> Using this method for our reference materials, we observed a chemical shift of about 2 eV from CoO (Co<sup>2+</sup>) to Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> (Co<sup>2.67+</sup>). A chemical shift of 3 eV is usually observed between absorption&nbsp;Co-edge positions in oxide materials with Co<sup>2+</sup> and Co<sup>3+</sup>; see for example, refs  <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref34" aria-label="reference 34">(34)</a> and  <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref35" aria-label="reference 35">(35)</a>. Assuming this correlation, we revealed a change in the valence state of Co during Na extraction from O3-Na<sub>0.95</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> between nearly Co<sup>2.2+</sup> and Co<sup>3.0+</sup>. It is somewhat lower than the Co valence states, calculated from the current flow in the corresponding galvanostatic experiment. A comparison of the measured Co valence states from XAS and the calculated ones from electrochemistry is presented in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/suppl_file/am8b11609_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S5</a>. During subsequent Na insertion into the material at potentials down to 1.2 V versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na, Co was reduced to Co<sup>2.7+</sup> only. This observation is in agreement with a much smaller specific capacity upon cell discharging compared to cell charging. Further, cell discharging to 0.2 V leads to the initial Co<sup>2.1+</sup> state in an almost linear manner (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig11" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig11" id="" class=" internalNav">11</a>a, inset).</div><figure id="fig11" data-index="11" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 11</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/medium/am-2018-11609g_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0003.jpeg" id="gr11" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 11. (a) Normalized Co-K-edge operando absorption spectra of O3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> together with CoO and Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> as Co<sup>2+</sup> and Co<sup>2+</sup>/Co<sup>3+</sup> reference materials, respectively. Inset: Composition dependence of the energy position for the Co-K-edge of the O3-phase at 0.8 of the postedge intensity. (b) Normalized Ti-K-edge ex situ absorption spectra of Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> together with TiO<sub>2</sub> as the Ti<sup>4+</sup> reference material.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11609&amp;id=fig11"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">From the Ti-K-edge spectra of several Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> materials with different sodium contents, we derived information on how Ti is involved in the electrochemical reaction. All spectra were measured ex situ together with TiO<sub>2</sub>-rutile as a reference for Ti<sup>4+</sup> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig11" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig11" id="" class=" internalNav">11</a>b). First of all, they show the same energy at a normalized 0.8 of the postedge intensity, thus confirming that Ti<sup>4+</sup> is silent and does not take part in the desodiation and sodiation redox processes.</div><div class="NLM_p">The evolution of the average Co–O distances in Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, obtained from the Fourier transformations of the <i>k</i><sup>3</sup>-weighted Co-EXAFS data, is also nonlinear during Na extraction; see <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig12" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig12" id="" class=" internalNav">12</a>. For the pristine O3-Na<sub>0.95</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> crystal structure, the Co–O distance of 1.97(3) Å matches well with the NPD and synchrotron powder diffraction data and is in accordance with mainly the Co<sup>2+</sup> valence state, as detected in the XPS studies. Upon Na extraction from the structure and the transformation to P3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, the Co–O bond length decreases to 1.89(1) Å, indicating the oxidation of cobalt towards Co<sup>3+</sup> and even higher. The interatomic Co–(Co,Ti) distance of 2.93(1) Å in O3-Na<sub>0.95</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> is reduced to 2.86(1) Å in P3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and remained nearly constant for subsequent Na insertion (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig12" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig12" id="" class=" internalNav">12</a>). The Co–O bond length reaches the initial value of 1.97–2.00 Å, corresponding to mostly Co<sup>2+</sup>, upon Na intercalation only at the cut off cell potential of 0.2 V versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na.</div><figure id="fig12" data-index="12" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 12</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/medium/am-2018-11609g_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0004.jpeg" id="gr12" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 12. Changes in interatomic distances of Co–O and Co-(Co,Ti) in O3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> upon Na extraction and insertion, evaluated from in situ Co-EXAFS experiments. The coordination spheres up to 3.0 Å were considered for calculations. Detailed fitting results are given in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/suppl_file/am8b11609_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S2</a>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11609&amp;id=fig12"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec3_6" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i18" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i18"> Magnetization Measurements on O3- and P3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> at Different Sodiation Levels</h3><div class="NLM_p">Typical temperature dependences of the magnetization of investigated materials with 0.2 ≤ <i>x</i> ≤ 1 show paramagnetic-like behavior down to low temperatures (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig13" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig13" id="" class=" internalNav">13</a>) because the magnetic Co ions are diluted by the Ti ions. Above 100 K, the inverse susceptibilities follow the Curie–Weiss behavior with effective paramagnetic moments depending on the composition (<a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">Table </a><a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">1</a>). The positive Weiss constants for all samples indicate ferromagnetically interacting spins.</div><figure id="fig13" data-index="13" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 13</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/medium/am-2018-11609g_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0005.jpeg" id="gr13" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 13. Temperature dependence of the magnetization for different sodiation levels of O3 and P3 materials. The notation of samples is further explained in <a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">Table </a><a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">1</a>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11609&amp;id=fig13"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_table-wrap" id="tbl1"><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption"><div class="NLM_caption" id=""><div class="title2">Table 1.
