class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">2.28 (HS-Co<sup>2+</sup>&nbsp;+&nbsp;LS-Co<sup>3+</sup>)</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="NLM_table-wrap-foot" id="IDtable-wrap-foot-t1fn1"><div class="footnote" id="t1fn1"><sup><sup>a</sup></sup><p class="last">Theoretical spin-only moments μ<sub>eff</sub><sup>2</sup> = 2<i>S</i>(<i>S</i> + 1)μ<sub>B</sub><sup>2</sup> were calculated for different composition-dependent valence scenarios with HS-Co<sup>2+</sup> (d<sup>7</sup>, <i>S</i> = 3/2), HS-Co<sup>3+</sup> (d<sup>6</sup>, <i>S</i> = 2), LS-Co<sup>3+</sup> (d<sup>6</sup>, <i>S</i> = 0), and LS-Co<sup>4+</sup> (d<sup>5</sup>, <i>S</i> = 1/2).</p></div><div class="footnote" id="t1fn2"><sup><sup>b</sup></sup><p class="last">According to the XRD measurement, sample “<i>a</i>” corresponds to features of the P3-structure, sample “<i>b</i>” consists of about 85% O3- and 15% P3-forms, and sample “<i>c</i>” of 90% O3- and 10% of P3-forms.</p></div></div></div><div class="NLM_p">Although the effective paramagnetic moments are usually used to distinguish between different valence states of transition metals, the case of Co ions is not straightforward because of the orbital component, which is very typical for HS states, HS-Co<sup>2+</sup> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33 ref36'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref33 ref36" aria-label="reference 33 and 36">(33,36)</a> and HS-Co<sup>3+</sup> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37 ref38'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37 ref38" aria-label="reference 37 and 38">(37,38)</a> in oxides.</div><div class="NLM_p">In pristine O3-Na<sub>0.95</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, the effective moment of 3.35(2) μ<sub>B</sub>/f.u. is somewhat larger than the theoretical spin-only value of 2.82 μ<sub>B</sub>/f.u. for cobalt in the two HS valence states (<a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">Table </a><a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">1</a>), HS-Co<sup>2+</sup> (d<sup>7</sup>, <i>S</i> = 3/2) and HS-Co<sup>3+</sup> (d<sup>6</sup>, <i>S</i> = 2), but it may be augmented by the orbital components. Another possible valence scenario, namely, HS-Co<sup>2+</sup> and LS-Co<sup>3+</sup> (d<sup>6</sup>, <i>S</i> = 0), is also often observed in oxides, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref39" aria-label="reference 39">(39)</a> but would provide an even smaller effective moment of 2.60 μ<sub>B</sub>/f.u.</div><div class="NLM_p">The reduction of the Na content in the O3-phase, which induces the transformation into the P3 structure, leads to a strong decrease in the effective moment; see <a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">Table </a><a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">1</a>. Removal of about 0.5 Na/f.u. must result in a Co<sup>3+</sup> valence state solely. Further Na removal can lead to further oxidation of cobalt to Co<sup>4+</sup>, like in Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>CoO<sub>2</sub>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4 ref7'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref4 ref7" aria-label="reference 4 and 7">(4,7)</a> to partial oxidation of oxygen atoms <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref40" aria-label="reference 40">(40)</a> or to both. The best agreement between the measured and calculated values for the effective paramagnetic moment is reached under an assumption of coexisting LS-Co<sup>3+</sup> (d<sup>6</sup>, <i>S</i> = 0) and LS-Co<sup>4+</sup> (d<sup>5</sup>, <i>S</i> = 1/2) ions. The experimental effective moment of 0.96(2) μ<sub>B</sub>/f.u. in the initial P3-Na<sub>0.65</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> corresponds rather to the coexistence of LS-Co<sup>3+</sup> and HS-Co<sup>2+</sup> (<a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">Table </a><a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">1</a>), whereas the HS-Co<sup>3+</sup>/HS-Co<sup>2+</sup> scenario with 3.3 μ<sub>B</sub>/f.u. would significantly exceed the measured moment. Sodium removal from the P3 structure with preserving the structure symmetry also decreases the effective moment, which matches satisfactorily with the LS-Co<sup>3+</sup>/LS-Co<sup>4+</sup> scenario, similar to the O3 case. The subsequent sodium insertion at the cut off voltage of 1.6 V versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na preserves the P3-form as well. The experimental paramagnetic moment is consistent with the LS-Co<sup>3+</sup>/LS-Co<sup>4+</sup> case. Further sodium insertion, accompanied by the reappearance of the O3 structure, increases the effective moment. For the composition Na<sub>0.85</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> that contains 85% O3- and 15% P3-forms, according to the XRD analysis, the experimental moment of 2.81 μ<sub>B</sub>/f.u. matches well the combination of HS-Co<sup>2+</sup> + HS-Co<sup>3+</sup> producing 2.97 μ<sub>B</sub>/f.u. (<a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">Table </a><a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">1</a>). If we assume the presence of LS-Co<sup>3+</sup> together with HS-Co<sup>2+</sup>, a much lower value of 2.28 μ<sub>B</sub>/f.u. would be obtained.</div><div class="NLM_p last">Altogether, from the magnetization data, we infer the coexistence of LS-Co<sup>3+</sup>/HS-Co<sup>2+</sup> or LS-Co<sup>3+</sup>/LS-Co<sup>4+</sup> for the P3-phase dependent on the sodium content and HS-Co<sup>2+</sup>/HS-Co<sup>3+</sup> for the O3-phase. This description is in agreement with the structural data, especially with the change of the Co–O bond lengths during the transformation of the P3 structure into the O3 structure.</div></div><div id="sec3_7" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i20" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i20"> <i>Quasi</i>-Symmetrical Cell Setting with P3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> Anode and O3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> Cathode</h3><div class="NLM_p">As deposition and dissolution of metallic sodium in Na ion batteries is accompanied by dendritic growth and undermines stable operation, a suitable replacement for sodium metal anodes is actively sought after. As the most popular alternative, carbonaceous anode materials also suffer from these safety concerns because their low sodiation potential can lead to sodium plating. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41" aria-label="reference 41">(41)</a> Moreover, they display a large irreversible capacity loss in the first cycle and often require presodiation. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref42" aria-label="reference 42">(42)</a> In contrast to that, different Na contents in the O3- and P3-phases facilitate the usage of these materials as cathode (O3) and anode (P3) even in the as-prepared form without further electrochemical treatment. The construction of a <i>quasi</i>-symmetrical cell, where sodium is removed from the O3 modification and inserted into the P3 modification, leads to a full sodium-ion battery without metallic sodium. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig14" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig14" id="" class=" internalNav">14</a> shows the preliminary results for such a cell under galvanostatic cycling under nonoptimized conditions.</div><figure id="fig14" data-index="14" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 14</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/medium/am-2018-11609g_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0006.jpeg" id="gr14" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 14. Galvanostatic cycling of a <i>quasi</i>-symmetric two-electrode full cell containing an O3 cathode and a P3 anode for the first, third, and fifth cycles in the potential window of 3.5–0.0 V.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11609&amp;id=fig14"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i21">Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The peculiarity of Co-containing oxides is associated with the ability of cobalt to easily change its valence state between Co<sup>2+</sup> and Co<sup>4+</sup> and further change the spin state within the given valence. The actual spin states of Co<sup>3+</sup> in simple oxides such as LaCoO<sub>3</sub> remain vividly debated, as three different possibilities exist: LS (<i>S</i> = 0), HS (<i>S</i> = 2), and intermediate-spin (IS, <i>S</i> = 1) states.</div><div class="NLM_p">Changes in the valence and spin states of cobalt are central to the stability of different structure types because significant changes in the Co–O bond lengths occur and induce structural transformations. These transformations affect the applications of Co-based materials. The three-layered rhombohedral O3-NaCoO<sub>2</sub> is a typical example for such behavior. Na extraction from the initial O3 structure leads to a couple of intermediate single-layer O1 and P1 structures that are stabilized at intermediate sodium contents, whereas lower sodium content brings the system back to the three-layer rhombohedral structure O3. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref43" aria-label="reference 43">(43)</a> Magnetization data for desodiated Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>CoO<sub>2</sub> materials in the paramagnetic region mostly support the simple picture of localized charges with the LS Co<sup>3+</sup> (<i>S</i> = 0) and Co<sup>4+</sup> (<i>S</i> = 1/2) ions. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref43" aria-label="reference 43">(43)</a> Interestingly, desodiated compositions of two-layered P2-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>CoO<sub>2</sub> show similar magnetism with the LS Co<sup>3+</sup> and Co<sup>4+</sup> ions.</div><div class="NLM_p">In contrast to Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>CoO<sub>2</sub>, the case of Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> is more complicated, as the valence state of Co varies from Co<sup>2+</sup> for the fully sodiated state (O3 structure) to Co<sup>4+</sup>/Co<sup>3+</sup> for a sodium-poor state (P3 structure). This change may lead to a breakdown of the layered crystal structure because the ionic radii of Co<sup>2+</sup> (0.745 Å) and Co<sup>4+</sup> (0.53 Å) in the octahedral oxygen surrounding differ drastically. However, Ti ions significantly improve the structural stability and preserve not only the layered nature of the structure but also its rhombohedral symmetry. No monoclinic intermediates were detected upon Na extraction, in contrast to similar materials with 50% Co and 50% of transition metals other than Ti. For example, O3-NaCo<sub>0.5</sub>Fe<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> shows a complex structural behavior with several phase transformations that involve the ordering of Na vacancies during desodiation. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref44" aria-label="reference 44">(44)</a> Both transition metals Co and Fe are electrochemically active, implying that the first oxidation of Co at the beginning of desodiation is followed by an oxidation of Fe. Different behavior is reported for P2-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (space group <i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub>/<i>mmc</i>), <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15" aria-label="reference 15">(15)</a> where no structural transformations were detected by ex situ XRD studies at partially desodiated states.</div><div class="NLM_p">Upon desodiation, HS-Co<sup>2+</sup> in O3-NaCo<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> transforms quickly into LS-Co<sup>3+</sup> with a smaller ionic radius, leading to a negative unit cell volume change, in disagreement with the expectation of HS-Co<sup>3+</sup> with a higher ionic radius. The origin of this transformation may be understood from further density functional theory calculations.</div><div class="NLM_p">The influence of the crystal structure and the valence and spin states of Co in Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> on the volume of the Co-coordinating oxygen octahedra can be visualized as a correlation diagram (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig15" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig15" id="" class=" internalNav">15</a>). It depicts the size of the (Co,Ti)O<sub>6</sub>-octahedra depending on the Na content in Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> according to the operando XRD experiments, together with the theoretical values for regular CoO<sub>6</sub>-octahedra with different Co valence and spin states. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32" aria-label="reference 32">(32)</a> At <i>x</i>(Na) ≥ 0.5, the O3 structure with HS-Co<sup>2+</sup> as a major part and HS-Co<sup>3+</sup> as a minor part as well as the P3 structure with LS-Co<sup>3+</sup> as a major part and HS-Co<sup>2+</sup> as a minor part exist. At <i>x</i>(Na) ≤ 0.5, only P3 with LS-Co<sup>3+</sup> and LS-Co<sup>4+</sup> is stable.</div><figure id="fig15" data-index="15" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 15</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/medium/am-2018-11609g_0007.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0007.jpeg" id="gr15" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 15. Volume of the (Co,Ti)O<sub>6</sub> octahedra, extracted from operando XRD experiments, at varying <i>x</i>(Na) in Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, which were calculated from GCPL measurements. The filled and empty symbols correspond to cell charging and discharging, respectively, in different experiments. The squares are related to the O3-forms and the circles to the P3-forms. The dotted horizontal lines show the theoretical values for regular CoO<sub>6</sub> octahedra. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32" aria-label="reference 32">(32)</a></p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/asset/images/large/am-2018-11609g_0007.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11609&amp;id=fig15"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">During subsequent sodiation of the highly oxidized P3-form, the first voltage region down to 2 V versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na corresponds to the transformation of LS-Co<sup>4+</sup>/LS-Co<sup>3+</sup> to mostly LS-Co<sup>3+</sup> while preserving the P3-structure. The O3-form with HS-Co<sup>2+</sup> is not formed at this voltage. Only below 1 V, the O3-form starts to arise. Despite the fact that the O3 → P3 transformation upon desodiation involves gliding of the MO<sub>2</sub> slabs (1/3, 2/3, 0) and is kinetically more impeded than the ordinary Na extraction from the P2- or P3-forms, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref45" aria-label="reference 45">(45)</a> no significant voltage hysteresis was observed in the O3 materials at moderate current rates. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref10" aria-label="reference 10">(10)</a> Therefore, the observed large voltage hysteresis during the P3 → O3 transformation in Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> is most probably related to kinetically inhibited spin transformations of Co because Ti does not participate in the reduction process. The change in diffusion paths occurring at the P3 → O3 transformation may contribute to the potential drop, but cannot be its only cause, because several other layered materials with a similar sequence of phase transformations do not show big polarization. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2 ref46'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref2 ref46" aria-label="reference 2 and 46">(2,46)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">Note that the other layered form of Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, P2-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, exhibits only a small potential hysteresis of 0.3 V at charging–discharging. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15" aria-label="reference 15">(15)</a> The lattice parameter <i>a</i> ≈ 2.83 Å (<i>P</i>6<sub>3</sub>/<i>mmc</i>) indicates predominance of LS-Co<sup>3+</sup> in the initial state. Unfortunately, the exact Na content and structural changes upon Na removal from this P2-form have not been reported and will be an interesting topic for future investigation.</div><div class="NLM_p">Another explanation for the voltage hysteresis might be migration of Ti ions from the slabs to the intersheet space of the crystal structure, as observed in layered Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>TiO<sub>2</sub> during Na removal and insertion. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref47" aria-label="reference 47">(47)</a> However, our structural investigations revealed the similarity of the sodiation and desodiation mechanisms and speak against Ti atoms in the interlayer space, see <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig10" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig10" id="" class=" internalNav">10</a> and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/suppl_file/am8b11609_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S3</a>.</div><div class="NLM_p">The third parameter, which may contribute to the voltage hysteresis, is mechanical stress. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref48" aria-label="reference 48">(48)</a> The lattice expansion upon the P3 → O3 transformation during the sodiation of P3-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> acts against the excess pressure in the electrochemical cell. As the inner cell pressure is a crucial factor for the functioning of the used Swagelok or coin test cells, designing a pressure-free control experiment is challenging.</div><div class="NLM_p last">Finally, we note that the complete insertion of Na into the O3 structure leads to the specific capacity of 180–200 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, which is much higher than the specific capacity reported for P2-Na<sub>0.66</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15" aria-label="reference 15">(15)</a></div></div><div id="sec5" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i22">Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">Two novel Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> materials with P3 (<i>R</i>3<i>m</i>) and O3 (<i>R</i>3̅<i>m</i>) layered structures were synthesized and studied as electrode materials in Na-ion batteries. These materials show not only some differences in the crystal structures, namely the prismatic (P3) and octahedral (O3) surrounding for the sodium atoms, but also differ in the electronic structures elucidated via the different valence- and spin-states of Co. A combination of HS-Co<sup>2+</sup>/HS-Co<sup>3+</sup> was detected in pristine O3, compared to HS-Co<sup>2+</sup>/LS-Co<sup>3+</sup> in P3. Both materials deliver high specific capacity values of 180–200 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>. During the desodiation process, O3 immediately transforms into P3. This transformation is accompanied by a significant negative volume change of about 5%. Na extraction from the P3-form occurs via a solid-solution mechanism without any symmetry change and appreciable volume deviations. Upon subsequent sodium insertion, a two-step process, coupled with a charge and a spin transition of Co as LS-Co<sup>3+</sup> to HS-Co<sup>2+</sup>/HS-Co<sup>3+</sup> was observed. At the end of the first voltage step of about 2 V, a composition P3-Na<sub><i>x</i>≈0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> with mostly LS-Co<sup>3+</sup> is reached, whereas further Na insertion below 1 V versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na is associated with the O3 formation exhibiting HS-Co<sup>2+</sup>/HS-Co<sup>3+</sup>. This large potential hysteresis is most probably of a kinetic origin. The Ti cations in both materials serve solely as a structure stabilizer without any electrochemical activity down to 0.2 V versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na. Different Na contents in both O3 and P3 materials and the large potential hysteresis allow the construction of a Na-free <i>quasi</i>-symmetrical full cell with an O3 cathode and a P3 anode. As a final remark, we found that layered sodium transition metal oxides have to be carefully examined regarding both the oxidation and the spin states of the involved transition metals to understand their electrochemical behavior. Only these profound insights will allow the best choice of suitable compositions and advanced tuning of their properties for future energy-storage applications.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i23">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acsami.8b11609" class="ext-link">10.1021/acsami.8b11609</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Structural parameters of O3- and P3-phases, cycling performance, comparison of Na content from Rietveld refinement and GCPL measurements, EXAFS fitting results, and comparison of Co valence states from XAS edge and GCPL measurements (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/suppl_file/am8b11609_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11609/suppl_file/am8b11609_si_001.pdf">am8b11609_si_001.pdf (1.01 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="testing" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b11609" data-url="https://widgets.figshare.com/static/figshare.js" id="figshare-widget"></div><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="85b54935-30e9-4058-a6d2-0b40fb754a85" class="mb-4">

                        cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Slater, Michael D.; Kim, Donghan; Lee, Eungje; Doeff, Marca; Johnson, Christopher S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The status of ambient temp. sodium ion batteries is reviewed in light of recent developments in anode, electrolyte and cathode materials.  These devices, although early in their stage of development, are promising for large-scale grid storage applications due to the abundance and very low cost of sodium-contg. precursors used to make the components.  The engineering knowledge developed recently for highly successful Li ion batteries can be leveraged to ensure rapid progress in this area, although different electrode materials and electrolytes will be required for dual intercalation systems based on sodium.  In particular, new anode materials need to be identified, since the graphite anode, commonly used in lithium systems, does not intercalate sodium to any appreciable extent.  A wider array of choices is available for cathodes, including high performance layered transition metal oxides and polyanionic compds.  Recent developments in electrodes are encouraging, but a great deal of research is necessary, particularly in new electrolytes, and the understanding of the SEI films.  The engineering modeling calcns. of Na-ion battery energy d. indicate that 210 Wh kg-1 in gravimetric energy is possible for Na-ion batteries compared to existing Li-ion technol. if a cathode capacity of 200 mAh g-1 and a 500 mAh g-1 anode can be discovered with an av. cell potential of 3.3 V.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGojsFXLPEQzILVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lifGWT1o5obbQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XntlSnurc%253D&amp;md5=fa5d7d089d261a40896cb6b03e88bfbe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1039/c4ee03192j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, M.                         cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A comprehensive review of sodium layered oxides: powerful cathodes for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Han, Man Huon; Gonzalo, Elena; Singh, Gurpreet; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">81-102</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The room temp. Na-ion secondary battery has been under focus lately due to its feasibility to compete against the already well-established Li-ion secondary battery.  Although there are many obstacles to overcome before the Na-ion battery becomes com. available, recent research discoveries corroborate that some of the cathode materials for the Na-ion battery have indeed indisputable advantages over its Li-ion counterparts.  In this publication, a comprehensive review of layered oxides (NaTMO2, TM = Ti, V, Cr, Mn, Fe, Co, Ni, and a mixt. of 2 or 3 elements) as a viable Na-ion battery cathode is presented.  Single TM systems are well characterized not only for their electrochem. performance but also for their structural transitions during the cycle.  Binary TM systems are investigated in order to address issues regarding low reversible capacity, capacity retention, operating voltage, and structural stability.  As a consequence, some materials already have reached an energy d. of 520 mW h g-1, which is comparable to that of LiFePO4.  Furthermore, some ternary TM systems retained more than 72% of their capacity along with over 99.7% Coulombic efficiency for 275 cycles.  The goal of this review is to present the development of Na layered oxide materials in the past as well as the state of the art today in order to emphasize the compatibility and durability of layered oxides as powerful candidates for Na-ion battery cathode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpwo96Ash7WNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lifGWT1o5obbQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitVCrsLjE&amp;md5=d938be66a2a0948e3d2f589b803dbf76</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1016/0167-2738(81)90076-x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Delmas, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Braconnier, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fouassier, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hagenmuller, P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrochemical intercalation of sodium in Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>CoO<sub>2</sub> bronzes</span>. <i>Solid State Ionics</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">1981</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3-4</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">165</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">169</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical intercalation of sodium in sodium cobalt oxide (NaxCoO2) bronzes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Delmas, Claude; Braconnier, Jean Jacques; Fouassier, Claude; Hagenmuller, Paul</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Solid State Ionics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1981</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3-4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">165-9</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SSIOD3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0167-2738</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">The chem. study of the NaxCoO2 system (0.5 ≤ x ≤1) has shown previously the existence of bronze-type phases with layer structure.  In each material, the lattice is built up by sheets of edge-sharing CoO6 octahedra allowing Na+ to be intercalated with trigonal prismatic surrounding (AABBCC or AABB packing of O) for small values of x and octahedral environment (ABCABC packing of O) for larger ones.  Discharge potentials (2.0 &lt; V &lt; 3.5 V) were measured as a function of the compn.  The electrochem. intercalation of Na in all these materials is reversible within their existence range.  During the electrochem. intercalation, a reversible charge is obsd. between phases having AABBCC and ABCABC packing of O.  This behavior can be explained by the relatively small displacement of the sheets.  In contrast, for the material with AABB packing of O, no transition occurs because a packing change requires breaking of Co-O bonds, which is apparently impossible at room temp.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrkktugvcleXLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lie42YCOhSy-g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaL3MXlvFChtL8%253D&amp;md5=3f450557c36835cd364b52b72a333f93</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1103/physrevlett.92.247001"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Foo, M.                         cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Large thermoelectric power in NaCo2O4 single crystals</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Terasaki, I.; Sasago, Y.; Uchinokura, K.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review B: Condensed Matter</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1997</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">56</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">20</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">R12685-R12687</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PRBMDO</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0163-1829</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Physical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We measured and analyzed the transport properties of single-crystal NaCo2O4, which is a metallic transition-metal oxide consisting of a two-dimensional triangle lattice of Co.  Reflecting the crystal structure, the resistivity is highly anisotropic between in- and out-of-plane directions, and the in-plane resistivity is as low as 200 μΩ cm at 300 K. Most strikingly, the in-plane thermoelec. power of NaCo2O4 is about 100 μV/K at 300 K, which is nearly ten times larger than that of typical metals.  The large thermoelec. power and the low resistivity suggest that NaCo2O4 is a potential thermoelec. material.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpYqXRsoeYTqrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lie42YCOhSy-g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK2sXnsFentrc%253D&amp;md5=03b1343a7ed6db2f4aaf0abba506c464</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1038/nmat1669"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Viciu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Foo, M.                         cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Large enhancement of the thermopower in NaxCoO2 at high Na doping</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lee, Minhyea; Viciu, Liliana; Li, Lu; Wang, Yayu; Foo, M. L.; Watauchi, S.; Pascal, R. A., Jr.; Cava, R. J.; Ong, N. P.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2006</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Research on the oxide perovskites has uncovered electronic properties that are strikingly enhanced compared with those in conventional metals.  Examples are the high crit. temps. of the cuprate superconductors and the colossal magnetoresistance in the manganites.  The conducting layered cobaltate NaxCoO2 exhibits several interesting electronic phases as the Na content x is varied, including water-induced supercond. and an insulating state that is destroyed by field.  Initial measurements showed that, in the as-grown compn., NaxCoO2 has moderately large thermopower S and cond. σ.  However, the prospects for thermoelec. cooling applications faded when the figure of merit Z was found to be small at this compn. (0.6&lt;x&lt;0.7).  Here we report that, in the poorly explored high-doping region x&gt;0.75, S undergoes an even steeper enhancement.  At the crit. doping xp∼0.85, Z (at 80 K) reaches values ∼40 times larger than in the as-grown crystals.  We discuss prospects for low-temp. thermoelec. applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGplMQADzYFC-7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lie42YCOhSy-g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD28XmsVGjsbo%253D&amp;md5=a9a12b6e2282c2f10c9c9fd4507b4dc9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1038/nature01450"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Takada, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sakurai, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Takayama-Muromachi, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Izumi, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dilanian, R.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Superconductivity in two-dimensional CoO2 layers</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Takada, Kazunori; Sakurai, Hiroya; Takayama-Muromachi, Eiji; Izumi, Fujio; Dilanian, Ruben A.; Sasaki, Takayoshi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature (London, United Kingdom)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Since the discovery of high-transition-temp. (high-Tc) supercond. in layered copper oxides, many researchers have searched for similar behavior in other layered metal oxides involving 3d transition metals, such as cobalt and nickel.  Such attempts have so far failed, with the result that the copper oxide layer is thought to be essential for supercond.  Here, the authors report that NaxCoO2·yH2O (x ≈ 0.35, yr ≈ 1.3) is a superconductor with a Tc of about 5 K.  This compd. consists of two-dimensional CoO2 layers sepd. by a thick insulating layer of Na+ ions and H2O mols.                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">P2-type Nax[Fe1/2Mn1/2]O2 made from earth-abundant elements for rechargeable Na batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yabuuchi, Naoaki; Kajiyama, Masataka; Iwatate, Junichi; Nishikawa, Heisuke; Hitomi, Shuji; Okuyama, Ryoichi; Usui, Ryo; Yamada, Yasuhiro; Komaba, Shinichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>

Mn- and Fe-based cathode materials, such as LiMn2O4 and LiFePO4, are used in large-scale batteries for elec. vehicles.  Mn and Fe are abundant elements in the Earth's crust, but Li is not.  In contrast to Li, Na is an attractive charge carrier from elemental abundance.  Recently, some layered materials, where Na can be electrochem. and reversibly extd./inserted, have been reported.  However, their reversible capacity is typically limited to 100 mA-h/g.  Herein, the authors report a new electrode material, P2-Na2/3[Fe1/2Mn1/2]O2, that delivers 190 mA-h/g of reversible capacity in Na cells with the electrochem. active Fe3+/Fe4+ redox.  These results will contribute to the development of rechargeable batteries from the earth-abundant elements operable at room temp.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoHU9moaXs6J7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljshzJ39vFbfA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38Xmt1GqtL8%253D&amp;md5=519efcb60bb0a6fd4843546d51921eb7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1021/ic300357d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yabuuchi, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nakayama, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ogata, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ishikawa, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nakai, I.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Study on the Reversible Electrode Reaction of Na<sub>1-x</sub>Ni<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> for a Rechargeable Sodium-Ion Battery</span>. <i>Inorg.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Study on the Reversible Electrode Reaction of Na1-xNi0.5Mn0.5O2 for a Rechargeable Sodium-Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Komaba, Shinichi; Yabuuchi, Naoaki; Nakayama, Tetsuri; Ogata, Atsushi; Ishikawa, Toru; Nakai, Izumi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Inorganic Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">51</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6211-6220</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">INOCAJ</span>;

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 (space group: R3‾m), having an O3-type (α-NaFeO2 type) structure according to the Delmas' notation, is prepd. by a solid-state method.  The electrochem. reactivity of NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 is examd. in an aprotic sodium cell at room temp.  The NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 electrodes can deliver ca. 105-125 mAh g-1 at rates of 240-4.8 mA g-1 in the voltage range of 2.2-3.8 V and show 75% of the initial reversible capacity after 50 charge/discharge cycling tests.  In the voltage range of 2.2-4.5 V, a higher reversible capacity of 185 mAh g-1 is achieved; however, its reversibility is insufficient because of the significant expansion of interslab space by charging to 4.5 V vs. sodium.  The reversibility is improved by adding fluoroethylene carbonate into the electrolyte soln.  The structural transition mechanism of Na1-xNi0.5Mn0.5O2 is also examd. by an ex situ X-ray diffraction method combined with X-ray absorption spectroscopy (XAS).  The staking sequence of the [Ni0.5Mn0.5]O2 slabs changes progressively as sodium ions are extd. from the crystal lattice.  It is obsd. that the original O3 phase transforms into the O'3, P3, P'3, and P3'' phases during sodium extn.  XAS measurement proves that NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 consists of divalent nickel and tetravalent manganese ions.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical properties of P2-Na2/3[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2 cathode material for sodium ion batteries when cycled in different voltage ranges</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Hong; Yang, Bingjian; Liao, Xiao-Zhen; Xu, Jing; Yang, Dezhi; He, Yu-Shi; Ma, Zi-Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">P2-type Na2/3[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2 cathode material has been synthesized via spray drying method and a two-step solid state process.  Electrochem. behavior of the prepd. material as cathode material for sodium-ion battery was investigated in different charge-discharge voltage ranges.  The results indicated that the cycling performance of the P2-Na2/3[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2 cathode greatly depended on the voltage window.  The material showed excellent reversibility between 2.0 V and 4.0 V with reversible capacity of 86 mA-h/g (0.1C) and 77 mA-h/g (1C).  X-ray diffraction analyses indicated that crystal structure of the P2-type Na2/3[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2 could be well maintained after long-term cycling in 2.0-4.0 V.  When the upper limiting voltage was increased to 4.5 V, the crystal structure of P2-Na2/3[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2 was irreversibly damaged due to over-extn. of Na+ in 4.0-4.5 V.  On the other hand, when the cycling voltage range was between 1.6 V and 3.8 V, the discharge capacities increased to 135 mA-h/g (0.1C) and 108 mA-h/g (1C), resp.  However, the cycling stability in 1.6-3.8 V was not as excellent as that in 2.0-4.0 V.  This maybe due to the lattice stress caused by the over-insertion of Na+ in the structure at lower voltage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpWdaIm0VHqHbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljshzJ39vFbfA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhvFGrt77K&amp;md5=0e04a11a1b28e1d8418f17c4be8d330f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1021/jp406433z"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tamaru, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Okubo, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yamada, A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrode Properties of P2-Na<sub>2/3</sub>Mn<sub>y</sub>Co<sub>1-y</sub>O<sub>2</sub> as Cathode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J. We present Na2/3Co1/2Ti1/2O2 as a potential new cathode material for sodium-ion batteries.  The crystal features and morphol. of the pristine powder were characterized by X-ray diffraction (XRD) and SEM (SEM).  The cathode material is evaluated in galvanostatic charge-discharge and galvanostatic intermittent titrn. tests, as well as ex-situ X-ray diffraction anal.  Synthesized by a high-temp. solid state reaction, Na2/3Co1/2Ti1/2O2 crystallizes in P2-type structure with P63/mmc space group. The ex-situ XRD measurements confirmed the reversibility and stability of the material.  No structural changes were obsd. in the XRD patterns, and the P2-type structure was stable during the charge/discharge process between 2.0 and 4.2 V vs.  Na+/Na.  These outcomes will contribute to the progress of developing low cost electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpfkWjtriiohbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8Wv31kgMYKg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXpsFygtQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=5cead8271c39c08ac8aa3fd55e20a608</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1126/sciadv.aar6018"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, P.-F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, H.-R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, Y.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.-N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Y.-G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na<sup>+</sup>/vacancy disordering promises high-rate Na-ion batteries</span>. <i>Sci.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-performance symmetric sodium-ion batteries using a new, bipolar O3-type material, Na0.8Ni0.4Ti0.6O2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guo, Shaohua; Yu, Haijun; Liu, Pan; Ren, Yang; Zhang, Tao; Chen, Mingwei; Ishida, Masayoshi; Zhou, Haoshen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Based on low-cost and rich resources, sodium-ion batteries have been regarded as a promising candidate for next-generation energy storage batteries in the large-scale energy applications of renewable energy and smart grids.  However, there are some crit. drawbacks limiting its application, such as safety and stability problems.  In this work, a stable sym. sodium-ion battery based on the bipolar, active O3-type material, Na0.8Ni0.4Ti0.6O2, is developed.  This bipolar material shows a typical O3-type layered structure, contg. two electrochem. active transition metals with redox couples of Ni4+/Ni2+ and Ti4+/Ti3+, resp.  This Na0.8Ni0.4Ti0.6O2-based sym. cell exhibits a high av. voltage of 2.8 V, a reversible discharge capacity of 85 mA h g-1, 75% capacity retention after 150 cycles and good rate capability.  This full sym. cell will greatly contribute to the development of room-temp. sodium-ion batteries with a view towards safety, low cost and long life, and it will stimulate further research on sym. cells using the same active materials as both cathode and anode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqmF3B7AwSKZ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8Wv31kgMYKg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXitlamsLw%253D&amp;md5=ea808bbce1fe8dbd563aeb8d25a9e1e7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Carmichael, R.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanostructured Ti-based anode materials for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mei, Yueni; Huang, Yunhui; Hu, Xianluo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">With the shortage of fossil energy and global climate change, renewable energy sources offer the most promising solns. to these challenges.  However, the intermittence of energy sources such as solar and wind requires sustainable energy storage technologies.  Nowadays, electrochem. energy storage technologies and applications have attracted much attention, including portable elec. devices, elec. vehicles and smart power grids.  Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) have been widely applied in these areas because of their safety, portability and high energy d.  Nevertheless, the resources of lithium are limited and the vast consumption of lithium has pushed up the price of lithium compds., urging people to search for resourceful materials.  Sodium can be a promising alternative due to its high abundance and low cost.  Furthermore, titanium-based materials have become a hot spot for anode materials in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), with their advantages of high safety and structural stability.  In this review, we summarize the recent advances in Ti-based anode materials for SIB applications.  We highlight the design and engineering of Ti-based nanoarchitectures, esp. emphasizing the effective enhancement in performance and the related sodium storage mechanism.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpa4N56ebVXIbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8Wv31kgMYKg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtVynt73M&amp;md5=40308f2ab8b2beb4f73c5fe67992c973</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1016/j.nima.2011.11.070"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hoelzel, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Senyshyn, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Juenke, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Boysen, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Schmahl, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fuess, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-resolution neutron powder diffractometer SPODI at research reactor FRM II</span>. <i>Nucl.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-resolution neutron powder diffractometer SPODI at research reactor FRM II</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hoelzel, M.; Senyshyn, A.; Juenke, N.; Boysen, H.; Schmahl, W.; Fuess, H.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nuclear Instruments &amp; Methods in Physics Research, Section A: Accelerators, Spectrometers, Detectors, and Associated Equipment</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">SPODI is a high-resoln. thermal neutron diffractometer at the research reactor Heinz Maier-Leibnitz (FRM II) esp. dedicated to structural studies of complex systems.  Unique features like a very large monochromator take-off angle of 155° and a 5 m monochromator-sample distance in its std. configuration achieve both high-resoln. and a good profile shape for a broad scattering angle range.  Two dimensional data are collected by an array of 80 vertical position sensitive 3He detectors.  SPODI is well suited for studies of complex structural and magnetic order and disorder phenomena at non-ambient conditions.  In addn. to std. sample environment facilities (cryostats, furnaces, magnet) specific devices (rotatable load frame, cell for elec. fields, multichannel potentiostat) were developed.  Thus the characterization of functional materials at in-operando conditions can be achieved.  In this contribution the details of the design and present performance of the instrument are reported along with its specifications.  A new concept for data redn. using a 2θ dependent variable height for the intensity integration along the Debye-Scherrer lines is introduced.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqVM-cL5upTcLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8Wv31kgMYKg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XktFemsg%253D%253D&amp;md5=f67a26cfea5ffb605e4b683e7468ba11</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.4028/www.scientific.net/msf.378-381.118"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Roisnel, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rodríquez-Carvajal, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">WinPLOTR: A Windows Tool for Powder Diffraction Pattern Analysis</span>. <i>Mater.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Determination of the kinetic parameters of mixed-conducting electrodes and application to the system lithium antimonide</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Weppner, W.; Huggins, R.     </div><div class="casAbstract">An electrochem. galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique is described which combines both transient and steady-state measurements to obtain kinetic properties of solid mixed-conducting electrodes, as well as thermodn. data.  The derivation of quantities such as the chem. and component diffusion coeffs., the partial cond., the mobility, the thermodn. enhancement factor, and the parabolic rate const. as a function of stoichiometry is presented.  A description of the factors governing the equil. of compn. gradients in such phases is included.  The technique is applied to the detn. of the kinetic parameters of Li3Sb, which has a narrow compn. range.  For Li2.9994Sb the chem. diffusion coeff. is 2 × 10-5 cm2-s-1 at 360°.  This value is quite high, due to a large thermodn. enhancement factor of 1.3 × 104.  The Li component diffusion coeff. at this compn. is 1.5 × 10-9 cm2-s3-1. The partial conductivity and elec. mobility of Li are 1.5 × 10-4 Ω-1-cm-1 and 3 × 10-8 cm2-V-1-s-1, resp., at the same stoichiometry and temp.  Because of the very large values of the chem. diffusion coeff. and the fact that 3 mols of Li can react per mol of Sb, this system may be of interest for use in new types of secondary batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqYkaAIzyKTuLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljKCP_VOXXHXQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Theoretical x-ray absorption fine structure standards</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Rehr, J.     </div><div class="casAbstract">Theor. x-ray absorption fine structure (XAFS) stds. were developed for arbitrary pairs of atoms throughout the periodic table (Z ≤94).  These std. XAFS spectra were obtained from ab initio single-scattering XAFS calcns., using an automated code, FEFF, which takes into account the most important features in current theories: (1) an exact treatment of curved-wave effects; (2) approx. mol. potentials derived from relativistic atoms; (3) a complex, energy-dependent self-energy; and (4) a well defined energy ref.  FEFF also yields tables of XAFS phases and amplitudes as well as mean-free paths.  Sample results are presented and compared with exptl. results and with earlier work.  These theor. stds. are competitive with exptl. stds., permitting XAFS anal. at lower wave nos. and yielding distance detns. typically better than 0.02 Å and coordination nos. typically better than 20%.  These stds. also provide theor. tests of chem. transferability in XAFS.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoaCLml2L5hqrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljKCP_VOXXHXQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK3MXktFOqs7w%253D&amp;md5=29b44173352f2b4934f81535ae3f6dca</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1063/1.1674508"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hildenbrand, D.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">New oxygenated bronzes of the formula NaxCoO2 (x.leq.1).     </div><div class="casAbstract">An investigation of the Na-Co-O system allows the isolation of 4 new bronze type phases with the formula NaxCoO2 (x ≤ 1).  The structure consists of sheets of octahedra (CoO2)n between which are inserted the Na ions.  Their structures differ from one another by the stacking sequence of the O layers, and by the distortions introduced as a result of the ordering of vacancies among the Na layers. Garcia; Kim, Jong-Gyu; Langell, Marjorie A.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Applied Surface Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2007</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">253</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The surface compn. and chem. environment of LiCoO2, hexagonal LiNiO2, cubic LiNiO2, and the mixed transition metal oxide, LiNi0.5Co0.5O2, have been detd. by Auger electron and x-ray photoelectron spectroscopies.  Although the LiCoO2 surface properties can easily be extrapolated from bulk compn., the Ni-contg. materials are less amenable to this procedure.  Their surface concn. tends to be depleted in Li relative to that of the bulk and shows an atypical chem. environment for the constituent elements.  The Ni 2p XPS photoemission suggests a near NiO-like selvedge through the XPS binding energies and satellite structure which are essentially identical to that of NiO - the spectrum appears fairly insensitive to Li concn.  Although there is little evidence for higher binding energy Ni3+ species or for an electron poor Ni2.δ+-derived band structure in the XPS, the lattice O is electron-rich and yields among the lowest binding energies reported for a transition metal oxide.  The Ni-contg. Li oxide selvedge is thus not simply NiO and the surface Li cations have a measurable effect on the electronic structure even in their more highly depleted levels.  This is explained in the context of the charge-transfer model of the oxide band structure.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGob-8tvLat_Z7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh31E3xKHtwQg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2sXitV2ku74%253D&amp;md5=b62674f809db287789c048a928e52349</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1103/physrevb.56.1290"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Saitoh, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mizokawa, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fujimori, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Abbate, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Takeda, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Takano, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electronic structure and magnetic states in La<sub>1–<i>x</i></sub>Sr<sub><i>x</i></sub>CoO<sub>3</sub> studied by photoemission and x-ray-absorption spectroscopy</span>. <i>Phys.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electronic structure of cobalt monoxide, lithium-doped cobalt monoxide, and lithium cobaltate (LiCoO2)</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Van Elp, J.; Wieland, J.     </div><div class="casAbstract">The electronic structure of LixCo1-xO (0.01 ≤ x ≤ 0.2), LiCoO2, and Co3O4 (1% Li) has been investigated using x-ray photoemissions spectroscopy (XPS), bremsstrahlung isochromat spectroscopy (BIS), and x-ray-absorption spectroscopy.  The exptl. results are compared with model cluster calcns.  The CoO band gap is of an intermediate character, between Mott-Hubbard-like and charge-transfer-like.  The first ionization state of CoO is therefore of strongly mmixed Co 3d and O 2p character.  Its local symmetry corresponds to 3T1g, similar to an intermediate-spin Co3+ state.  For x ≤ 0.2 the local Co electronic structure is similar to that of CoO.  However, LiCoO2 has a strongly reduced Co-O interat. distance, resulting in a ligand field strong enough to stabilize a Co3+ low-spin ground state.  LiCoO2 is an insulator with a gap of 2.7 eV.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">First-principles investigation of phase stability in LixCoO2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Van der Ven, A.; Aydinol, M. K.; Ceder, G.; Kresse, G.; Hafner, J.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review B: Condensed Matter and Materials Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1998</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">58</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2975-2987</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PRBMDO</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0163-1829</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Physical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, the phase diagram of LixCoO2 is calcd. from first principles for x ranging from 0 to 1.  Our calcns. indicate that there is a tendency for Li ordering at x=(1) /(2) in agreement with expt. [J. N. Reimers and J. R. Dahn, J. Electrochem. Soc. 139, 2091 (1992)].  At low Li concn., it is found that a staged compd. is stable in which the Li ions selectively segregate to every other Li plane leaving the remaining Li planes vacant.  The two-phase region obsd. is not found at high Li concn. and speculate that this two-phase region is caused by the metal-insulator transition that occurs at concns. slightly below x=1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrI0Ba4mxyjl7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljYocoUoehxnA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK1cXkvFSitL8%253D&amp;md5=1b398128aec22ae46f3192f7f9cc9ed5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1149/1.1379565"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Stevens, D. A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dahn, J. R.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Mechanisms of Lithium and Sodium Insertion in Carbon Materials</span>. <i>J. Electrochem.                 10.1149/1.1379565</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D148%26publication_year%3D2001%26pages%3DA803-A811%26journal%3DJ.%2BElectrochem.%2BSoc.%26author%3DD.%2BA.%2BStevens%26author%3DJ.%2BR.%2BDahn%26title%3DThe%2BMechanisms%2Bof%2BLithium%2Band%2BSodium%2BInsertion%2Bin%2BCarbon%2BMaterials%26doi%3D10.1149%252F1.1379565&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b11609&amp;doiOfLink=10.1149%2F1.1379565&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors compare the interactions of lithium and sodium with a range of carbon materials in electrochem. cells.  Through wide angle in situ x-ray scattering studies, both lithium and sodium can be inserted into the interlayer space in disordered carbon materials.  This insertion process is accompanied by an increase in the interlayer spacing in these materials.  Small-angle in situ scattering studies are presented to clearly show the insertion of lithium and sodium into nanopores within disordered hard carbons.  Also very little, if any, sodium can be inserted into graphitic materials in contrast to the large capacity seen for lithium insertion.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqOuo4QAURxurVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljYocoUoehxnA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD3MXlvFKntr0%253D&amp;md5=15fc03ac3de24271573ed94315375242</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1149/2.0091514jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Irisarri, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ponrouch, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Palacin, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review of hard carbon materials as neg. electrodes for sodium ion batteries is presented, covering not only the electrochem. performance but also the synthetic methods and microstructures.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Understanding the Structural Evolution and Redox Mechanism of a NaFeO2-NaCoO2 Solid Solution for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kubota, Kei; Asari, Takuya; Yoshida, Hiroaki; Yaabuuchi, Naoaki; Shiiba, Hiromasa; Nakayama, Masanobu; Komaba, Shinichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">33</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6047-6059</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have become promising candidates for large-scale energy-storage systems because of the abundant Na resources and they have attracted considerable academic interest because of their unique behavior, such as their electrochem. activity for the Fe3+/Fe4+ redox couple.  The high-rate performance derived from the low Lewis-acidity of the Na+ ions is another advantage of Na-ion batteries and has been demonstrated in NaFe1/2Co1/2O2 solns.  Here, a solid soln. of NaFeO2-NaCoO2 is synthesized and the mechanisms behind their excellent electrochem. performance are studied in comparison to those of their resp. end-members.  The combined anal. of operando X-ray diffraction, ex situ X-ray absorption spectroscopy, and d. functional theory (DFT) calcns. for Na1-xFe1/2Co1/2O2 reveals that the O3-type phase transforms into a P3-type phase coupled with Na+/vacancy ordering, which has not been obsd. in O3-type NaFeO2.  The substitution of Co for Fe stabilizes the P3-type phase formed by sodium extn. and could suppress the irreversible structural change that is usually obsd. in O3-type NaFeO2, resulting in a better cycle retention and higher rate performance.  Although no ordering of the transition metal ions is seen in the neutron diffraction expts., as supported by Monte-Carlo simulations, the formation of a superlattice originating from the Na+/vacancy ordering is found by synchrotron X-ray diffraction for Na0.5Fe1/2Co1/2O2, which may involve a potential step in the charge/discharge profiles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrIOOIWAWpvkLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljYocoUoehxnA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">NaFe0.5Co0.5O2 as high energy and power positive electrode for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yoshida, Hiroaki; Yabuuchi, Naoaki; Komaba, Shinichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochemistry Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">34</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">60-63</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">O3-type NaFeO2 is a promising candidate as pos. electrode materials for rechargeable Na batteries.  However, its reversible range of sodium extn. is relatively narrow (x = ca. 0.4 in Na1-xFeO2) because of the irreversible structural change, presumably assocd. with the iron migration into the adjacent tetrahedral sites in Na layers as we recently reported.  Herein, we report that cobalt-substituted NaFeO2 demonstrates excellent electrode performance in a non-aq. Na cell at room temp.  NaFe0.5Co0.5O2 delivers approx. 160 mAh g-1 of reversible capacity with relatively good capacity retention and excellent rate-capability in a voltage range of 2.5-4.0 V, resulting in reversible formation of Na0.3Fe0.5Co0.5O2.
